EXHIBIT A
SCOPE OF SERVICES
•
Contractor shall serve as a Hearing Officer for the City of San Mateo (“City”) and will provide 
professional services, including all work necessary for the effective handling of the City’s 
administrative hearings. 
•
The Hearing Officer conducts the public hearing, receives testimony and other evidence from 
all parties regarding the issues, and makes a written decision based on findings. 
•
The time frame for conducting hearings and issuing a decision is specified in the San Mateo 
Municipal Code, but generally a decision is issued within ten (10) days of the conclusion of 
the hearing. 
•
Findings and decisions are prepared by the Hearing Officer and issued to the involved 
parties. The number of hearings is expected to be few at the beginning of the assignment, 
and growing as the need expands.
•
The hearings may be virtual or in person at the discretion of the City.
•
The hearings are varied and may cover tenant relocation, health and safety, building and 
technical codes, San Mateo Municipal Code violations, and other matters as required by the 
San Mateo Municipal Code. 
•
The Hearing Officer may impose penalties, award enforcement costs, and/or issue 
corrective/abatement orders as authorized by the San Mateo Municipal Code. 
•
Hearing preparation may include review of the hearing and file materials, consultation with 
administrative staff, and knowledge of relevant City and State Code provisions.
•
Additional services such as issuing findings of facts, making recommendations, or making 
decisions in miscellaneous matters may also be included. 
•
The City shall provide at its sole expense a hearing room, use of copying equipment, case file 
packets, and documents. 
•
The City will also provide the necessary clerical support for the Hearing Officer to conduct 
City business.

INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as:
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate 
limit applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or 
the general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if 
CONTRACTOR has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no 
less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $1,000,000 per accident for bodily 
injury or disease. However, a Workers Compensation policy shall not be required if 
CONTRACTOR is a sole proprietor with no employees.
4. Professional Liability (Errors and Omissions): Insurance appropriate to the CONTRACTOR’s 
profession, with limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim, $2,000,000 aggregate
If the CONTRACTOR maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and 
shall be entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the CONTRACTOR.
Other Insurance Provisions
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:
Additional Insured Status
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the CONTRACTOR; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the CONTRACTOR including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the CONTRACTOR’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both 
CG 20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).
Primary Coverage
For any claims related to this contract, the CONTRACTOR’s insurance coverage shall be primary 
insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any 
insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or 
agents shall be excess of the CONTRACTOR’s insurance and shall not contribute with it.

PREPARED BY:
Parks and Recreation Department
MEETING DATE:
June 3, 2024 
SUBJECT:
Summer Camp Bus Transportation – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement for $109,730.80 with First Student Inc. to provide bus transportation services for City of San Mateo 
summer camps ; establish a contingency reserve of $10,973.00; and authorize the Director of Parks and Recreation to 
execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The City will host summer camps for over 1,400 participants ages 6-14 at Beresford Park and the Dr. Martin Luther King.  
During the eight  weeks of camp (June 17, 2024 through August 9, 2024), a key component will be field trips to locations 
such as Great America, Bel Mateo Bowl, Coyote Point, and Oakland Zoo. Buses are needed to transport participants. City 
staff issued a formal request for proposals (RFP) to five transportation companies and received a total of two responses. 
First Student Inc. was selected based on their ability to provide all services requested in the RFP scope. The other 
responsive vendor was unable to guarantee the necessary number of busses needed during the timeframe requested. First 
Student Inc. also successfully provided bus services for the City of San Mateo for summer camps in 2021, 2022, and 2023.
BUDGET IMPACT:
$109,730.80 plus a 10% potential contingency can be absorbed in the 2024 budget, and this agenda report is for contract 
authority only.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will not 
result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

Buses and Drivers shall meet the following conditions:  
1. Buses shall be certified by the State meeting requirements to transport school children a minimum 
of fifty-five (55) passengers with radio dispatch.  
2. The CONTRACTOR will meet all Federal and State rules, regulations, statutes, and ordinances, 
including proper driver’s license, bus certification, etc.  
3. Buses must be owned and/or leased by the CONTRACTOR. CONTRACTOR cannot subcontract 
services to another vendor.  
4. Liability insurance will be supplied by the CONTRACTOR. Copies of current insurance forms will be 
supplied by the CONTRACTOR.  
5. CONTRACTOR shall supply a copy of the written procedures for supplying alternate buses for buses 
which are disabled during transport.  
6. CONTRACTOR must supply recent references which are to include company name, address, and 
contact person with telephone number.  
7. Rental fee to include all gasoline charges. All maintenance of all vehicles, including any towing 
charges incurred by disabled buses, will be the responsibility of the CONTRACTOR.  
8. Any claims of damage must be reported to the Parks & Recreation Director. Any necessary repairs 
for the damage must be submitted in writing with cost estimated and pre-approved by the Parks & 
Recreation Director before repairs are started.  
9. Number of hours and buses are approximations and specific numbers are dependent on other 
factors. CONTRACTOR will be given as much advanced notice as possible, but not less than 24 hours.  
10. Radio communications between the bus drivers and the bus dispatcher must be in effect and 
operating at all times.  
11. The City reserves the right to cancel bus use for individual trips by giving 24 hours notice without 
penalty to San Mateo. CONTRACTOR should specify specific cancellation policy and who should be 
notified.  
12. A Program Supervisor riding the bus may request changes in the bus schedule or stops due to 
weather conditions or emergency situations. Driver must recognize staff requests for schedule changes 
and emergency stops and honor them.  
13. All prices include parking/toll charges. Buses must stay with the group for the duration of the 
individual trip unless otherwise directed by the Program Supervisor.  
14. All buses must stay with Parks & Recreation Camps and not go on another trip/location and leave 
our camp children at the program location without a bus. Bus and bus driver must stay with the camp 
event due to possible inclement weather or/an emergency situation.

mailed or electronically transferred no later than four (4) weeks upon receipt of the invoice (unless an 
error has occurred on the received invoice).  
 
Prices shall remain fixed and firm during the initial term of this contract; provided, however, that the 
company may offer incentive discounts from the fixed price to San Mateo at any time during the 
contractual term. 
 
 
If an error is found by CITY, CONTRACTOR will provide the process on how to remedy said error. After 
the error has been resolved, the CITY will pay out CONTRACTOR no later than four (4) weeks after that 
date

Contract for Services 
Page 12 of 16 
Rev 12/22 
EXHIBIT C 
INSURANCE REQUIREMENTS 
MINIMUM SCOPE OF INSURANCE 
Coverage shall be at least as broad as: 
1. Commercial General Liability (CGL):  Insurance Services Office (ISO) Form CG 00 01 12 07 
covering CGL on an “occurrence” basis, including products-completed operations, personal & 
advertising injury, with limits no less than $9,000,000 per occurrence. If a general aggregate limit 
applies, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the 
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.
2. Automobile Liability:  ISO Form Number CA 00 01 covering any auto (Code 1), or if Contractor 
has no owned autos, hired, (Code 8) and non-owned autos (Code 9), with limit no less than
$10,000,000 per accident for bodily injury and property damage.
3. Workers’ Compensation: as required by the State of California, with Statutory Limits, and 
Employer’s Liability Insurance with limit of no less than $5,000,000 per accident for bodily injury 
or disease.
4. Sexual Abuse or Molestation (SAM) Liability: If the work will include contact with minors, and 
the CGL policy referenced above is not endorsed to include affirmative coverage for sexual 
abuse or molestation, Contractor shall obtain and maintain a policy covering Sexual Abuse and 
Molestation with a limit no less than $1,000,000 per occurrence or claim.
If the contractor maintains higher limits than the minimums shown above, the City requires and shall be 
entitled to coverage for the higher limits maintained by the contractor. 
Other Insurance Provisions 
The insurance policies are to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions: 
Additional Insured Status 
The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents are to be covered as insureds on 
the auto policy for liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or borrowed by or on behalf 
of the Contractor; and on the CGL policy with respect to liability arising out of work or operations 
performed by or on behalf of the Contractor including materials, parts or equipment furnished in 
connection with such work or operations. General liability coverage can be provided in the form of an 
endorsement to the Contractor’s insurance (at least as broad as ISO Form CG 20 10, 11 85 or both CG 
20 10 and CG 20 37 forms if later revisions used).

Primary Coverage 
For any claims related to this contract, the Contractor’s insurance coverage shall be primary insurance 
as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents. Any insurance or self-
insurance maintained by the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, or agents shall be 
excess of the Contractor’s insurance and shall not contribute with it. 
Notice of Cancellation 
Each insurance policy required above shall provide that coverage shall not be canceled, except after 
thirty (30) days’ prior written notice (10 days for non-payment) has been given to the City. 
Waiver of Subrogation 
Contractor hereby grants to City a waiver of any right to subrogation which any insurer of said 
Contractor may acquire against the City by virtue of the payment of any loss under such insurance.  
Contractor agrees to obtain any endorsement that may be necessary to effect this waiver of 
subrogation, but this provision applies regardless of whether or not the City has received a 
waiver of subrogation endorsement from the insurer.   
Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions 
Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be declared to and approved by the City. The City may 
require the Contractor to purchase coverage with a lower deductible or retention or provide proof of 
ability to pay losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense expenses within the 
retention.   
Acceptability of Insurers 
Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of no less than A:VII, unless 
otherwise acceptable to the City. 
Verification of Coverage 
Contractor shall furnish the City with original certificates and amendatory endorsements or copies of 
the applicable policy language effecting coverage required by this clause.  All certificates and 
endorsements are to be received and approved by the City before work commences.  However, failure 
to obtain the required documents prior to the work beginning shall not waive the Contractor’s 
obligation to provide them.  The City reserves the right to require complete, certified copies of all 
required insurance policies, including endorsements required by these specifications, at any time.

SUBJECT:
2024-2025 School Crossing Guards – Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with the San Mateo-Foster City School District for school crossing guards in the amount not to 
exceed $78,000.00 and authorize Chief of Police Ed Barberini to execute the agreement in substantially the form 
presented.
BACKGROUND:
This is the annual agreement between the City of San Mateo and the San Mateo-Foster City School District to provide 
protection for school children, who are required to cross heavily traveled streets in the City. The streets are listed on 
Exhibit A.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The Police Department has budgeted for this agreement in the proposed 2024-2025 budget.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a physical 
change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

SCHOOL CROSSING GUARD AGREEMENT 
BETWEEN 
THE CITY OF SAN MATEO AND 
THE SAN MATEO-FOSTER CITY SCHOOL DISTRICT 
This agreement, made and entered into this day of                                       , by and between the 
City of San Mateo, a municipal corporation existing under the laws of the State of California, 
hereinafter "City," and the San Mateo-Foster City School District, hereinafter "District." 
 
WHEREAS, the City wants to assist the District in providing protection for school 
children who are required to cross heavily traveled streets in the City; and 
 
WHEREAS, some protection can be afforded by placing crossing guards at specific 
locations in the City; and 
 
WHEREAS, the District wishes to cooperate in providing protection for school pupils 
pursuant to Education Code section 45450 et seq., 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, it is agreed as follows: 
 
1. 
The District shall select, hire, and supervise crossing guards as necessary for each 
of the locations shown on Exhibit A to this agreement during the hours that pupils are walking to 
and from nearby schools on school days during the school year. Salaries and wages shall be at 
rates determined by the District and may include payment of a two or four hour minimum per 
shift, as shown on Exhibit A, in order to attract employees and effectively staff the positions. 
The crossing guards shall be considered, and shall in fact be, employees of the District for all 
purposes. 
 
2. 
The City agrees to reimburse District for wages and salaries paid by the District to 
the crossing guards for daily administrative costs incurred in providing the crossing guards so 
long as this reimbursement does not exceed that figure agreed to pursuant to paragraph 6 below. 
The reimbursement will include the payment of a two or four hour minimum per shift which will 
be clearly indicated on timecards for such occasions where such payment was necessary to 
effectively staff the position. 
 
3. 
Not later than thirty (30) days after the close of each calendar quarter, the District 
shall bill the City for reimbursement of the costs incurred for work in the previous quarter. The 
invoice to the City shall be submitted with appropriate supporting documentation such as 
employee timecards and payroll reports to substantiate the amount billed. Upon review of the 
invoice and supporting documentation, the City shall promptly pay the bill. 
 
4. 
The City and the District shall meet during the month of March of each year 
during the term of this agreement to allocate the City and District portions of the crossing guard 
expense. 
 
1 
135 of 465

--- page 136 ---
5. At any time during the term of this agreement, the District may request the City to
delete or add one or more locations from or to the list attached as Exhibit A hereto. If the City
determines, pursuant to California Traffic Manual section 10-08.2, that a location either should
or should not have a crossing guard, the parties may amend this Agreement to add or delete a
location from Exhibit A. If a location is added, the District shall promptly provide a crossing
guard at that location and bill the City appropriately for the location pursuant to this agreement.
If a location is deleted, the District shall promptly remove the crossing guard and immediately
cease billing for that location. During the meeting described in paragraph 4 above, the City and
the District shall discuss whether any location(s) should be added or deleted.

6. For fiscal year 2024 / 2025, the City’s contribution to the District for crossing
guards will not exceed $78,000. The hourly wage for the crossing guards will be $17.35,
commensurate with the City’s minimum wage. On January 1, 2025, the City’s minimum wage
will increase by CPI and crossing guard wages will be adjusted accordingly.

7. The District agrees to indemnify and hold the City harmless from any and all
claims, loss, liability, and damages in any way arising from the acts of the District or its
employees or agents, including the crossing guards, in the performance of this agreement.

8. The duty of the District to indemnify and hold harmless as set forth in this
agreement shall include the duty to defend as set forth in Civil Code section 2778.

9. Insurance. The District shall procure and maintain for the duration of the contract
insurance against claims for injuries to persons or damages to property which may arise from or
in connection with the performance of this Agreement.

Minimum Scope of Insurance. Coverage shall be as broad as:

a. Insurance Services Office Commercial General Liability coverage (occurrence Form
CG0001).

b. Workers’ Compensation Insurance as required by the State of California and Employer’s
Liability Insurance.

Minimum Limits of Insurance. District shall maintain limits no less than:

a. General Liability: $2,000,000 per occurrence for body injury, personal
(Including operations, injury and property damage. If Commercial
products and completed General Liability insurance or other form
operations.) with a general aggregate limit is used, either

the general aggregate limit shall apply
separately to this project/ location or the
general aggregate limit shall be twice the
required occurrence limits.

136 of 465


--- page 137 ---
b. Workers’ Compensation As required by the State of California.

c. Employers’ Liability $1,000,000 per accident or bodily injury or disease.

Deductibles and Self-Insured Retentions. Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be
declared to and approved by the City. At the option of the City, either: The insurer shall reduce
or eliminate such deductibles or self-insured retentions as respects the City, its elected and
appointed officials, employees and agents; or the District shall provide a financial guarantee
satisfactory to the City guaranteeing payment of losses and related investigations, claim
administration, and defense expenses.

Other Insurance Provisions. The general liability and automobile liability policies are to
contain, or be endorsed to contain, the following provisions:

a. The City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents, are to be
covered as insureds with respect to liability arising out of automobiles owned, leased, hired or
borrowed by or on behalf of the contractor; and with respect to liability arising out of work or
operations performed by or on behalf of the District including materials, parts or equipment
furnished in connection with such work or operations. General Liability coverage shall be
provided in the form of an Additional Insured endorsement (CG 20 10 11 85 or equivalent) to
the District’s insurance policy, or as a separate owner’s policy.

b. For any claims related to this project, District’s insurance coverage shall be
primary insurance as respects the City, its elected and appointed officials, employees, and agents.
Any insurance or self-insurance maintained by the City shall be excess of the District’s insurance
and shall not contribute with it.

c. Each insurance policy required by this clause shall be endorsed to state that
coverage shall not be canceled by either party, except after thirty (30) days prior written notice
has been provided to the City.

Acceptability of Insurers. District shall furnish the City with original certificates and
endorsements effecting coverage required by this clause. The endorsements should be on forms
provided by the City or on other than the City’s forms, provided those endorsements or policies
conform to the requirements. All certificates and endorsements are to be received and approved
by the City before work commences. However, failure to do so shall not operate as a waiver of
these insurance requirements. The City reserves the right to require complete certified copies of
all required insurance policies, including endorsements affecting the coverage required by these
specifications at any time.

If District is self-insured, District may satisfy this requirement by providing a written statement
that it is self-insured in the amounts set forth above.

Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Community Development Department
MEETING DATE:
June 03, 2024 
SUBJECT:
Community Development Permit Tracking Software – Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an Amendment to the Agreement with Tyler Technologies, Inc. to add payment processing services to the 
EnerGov Permitting and Licensing software; increase the annual service/maintenance fee by $1,080, for an annual total 
amount not to exceed $90,758.63; and authorize the Community Development Department Director to execute the 
Amendment in substantially the form provided. 
BACKGROUND:
In June 2013, City Council approved an agreement with Tyler Technologies, Inc. (Tyler Technologies) for permit and project 
tracking software (EnerGov) with related services and support in the amount of $900,172. The term of this agreement for 
Tyler Technologies’ services automatically renews each year unless terminated by either party. The continuing fees for 
Tyler Technologies’ services, including licensing and maintenance/support, are thereafter renewed and invoiced on an 
annual basis.  Here, staff requests approval to expand the scope of services from Tyler Technologies to include new credit 
card payment readers and software services in order to support online and in-person credit card payments (Tyler 
Payments).  Expanding this scope of services by Tyler Technologies requires Council approval, since the original scope of 
services approved by Council in 2013 did not include Tyler Payments.
For the past few years, the City Hall Permit Center has utilized a third-party credit card processing company, Persolvent, to 
process all permit financial transactions. Due to security enhancements and upgrades to EnerGov, the existing Persolvent 
card readers are no longer supported, not compatible with EnerGov, and do not meet current security standards. The 
result is that the existing card readers at the permit center counter no longer function to process credit card payments. In 
order to continue receiving credit card payments in-person at the Permit Center, new credit card readers with the latest 
security technologies are required. Staff compared the new Persolvent product with the Tyler Technologies product and 
determined that utilizing Tyler Payments would ensure compatibility and function with EnerGov, provide quality service to 
the public, and ensure that current security requirements were met.  
Having the ability to efficiently process payments both online and in-person is an essential function for building permit 
application processing. To achieve this, the City must have software and hardware that have current security and 
functional features. The move from Persolvent Payments to Tyler Payments will promote payment processing consistency 
with software that is compatible with the City’s current permitting database, EnerGov.  This change requires the purchase 
of six new credit card terminals and an amendment to an existing Agreement with Tyler Technologies in order to use the 
Tyler Payments software.  These new credit card terminals will meet current security standards and include touchless 
payment options, and will create a more user-friendly experience for our customers. 
140 of 465

--- page 141 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
BUDGET IMPACT:
The cost to purchase six new credit card terminals for the Permit Center will be $3,780, and the annual 
service/maintenance fee to use the Tyler Payments software will be $1,080. Transaction fees will be paid directly to Tyler 
Technologies by the payee as a pass-through expense, which is consistent with how transaction fees are currently 
processed. These additional costs to transition to Tyler Payments will be accounted for in Community Development’s 
Annual budget and would come from the Construction Services Fund. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
Approval of Amendment No. 1 is not subject to CEQA review under the “common sense” exemption, because it can be 
seen with certainty that there is no possibility that adding credit card payment processing services to an existing 
agreement may have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)

All meeting noticing requirements were met.

Payment Processing 
Agreement 
This Payment Processing Agreement (this “Processing Agreement”) is made and 
entered into by and between Tyler Technologies, Inc., a Delaware corporation (“Tyler”), 
and Client (the “Merchant”). 
 
1. ACKNOWLEDGEMENTS 
a. By executing this Processing Agreement or an accompanying Order Form, 
Merchant is contracting with Tyler to obtain Card processing services on 
Merchant’s behalf. 
b. Merchant acknowledges that Tyler contracts with a payment processor (a 
“Processor”), Members, and other third party providers to provide services under 
this Processing Agreement, and Merchant hereby consents to the use of such 
Processor, Members, and others to provide such services. 
c. To the extent elected in the Order Form, Tyler will provide Merchant with 
eCheck/ACH payment processing services for any eligible account as a turn-key 
solution or by presenting ACH Transactions in a NACHA Standard file 
submission to Merchant’s Originating Depository Financial Institution (ODFI) as 
agreed to in the Order Form. ACH Transactions and Card Transactions may 
collectively be referred to as “Transactions.” 
2. MEMBER BANK AGREEMENT 
REQUIRED 
a. When Merchant’s customers pay Merchant through Tyler, Merchant may be the 
recipient of a Card funded payment. The organizations that operate these Card 
systems (such as Visa U.S.A., Inc. and MasterCard International Incorporated; 
collectively, the “Associations”) require that Merchant (i) enter into a direct 
contractual relationship with an entity that is a member of the Association and (ii) 
agree to comply with Association Rules as they pertain to applicable Card 
Transactions that Merchant submits through Tyler. If Merchant accepts American 
Express, then Merchant agrees that the terms of Exhibit A shall apply. 
b. Merchant shall complete an application with the Member with which Tyler has 
contracted and execute an agreement with such Member (the “Member Bank 
Agreement”). By executing a Member Bank Agreement, Merchant is fulfilling the 
Association Rule of entering into a direct contractual relationship with a Member, 
and Merchant agrees to comply with Association Rules as they pertain to Card 
Transactions Merchant submits for processing through the Tyler service. 
c. Merchant acknowledges that Tyler may have agreed to be responsible for some 
of Merchant’s obligations to a Member for such Transactions as set forth in the 
Member Bank Agreement. Member may debit the Merchant Bank Account for 
148 of 465

--- page 149 ---
Exhibit 2 
3 
 
 
 
chargebacks, returns, refunds and other fees, however, in the event Member 
assesses any such chargeback, returns, refunds, or other fees to Tyler, Tyler 
may invoice the same to Merchant. 
3. SETTLEMENT AND CHARGEBACKS 
a. Merchants Bank Account. In order to receive funds, Merchant must maintain a 
bank account (the “Merchant Bank Account”) at a bank that is a member of the 
Automated Clearing House (“ACH”) system and the Federal Reserve wire 
system. Merchant agrees not to close the Merchant Bank Account without giving 
Tyler at least thirty (30) days’ prior written notice and substituting another bank 
account. Merchant is solely liable for all fees and costs associated with Merchant 
Bank Account and for all overdrafts. Tyler shall not be liable for any delays in 
receipt of funds or errors in bank account entries caused by third parties, 
including but not limited to delays or errors by the Member Bank or payment 
processor to Merchant Bank Account. 
b. Settlement. Transactions shall be settled according to the terms of the Member 
Bank Agreement using the account(s) which are designated by Merchant. 
c. Chargebacks, Returns and Refunds. Chargebacks, returns and refunds paid for 
ACH Transactions shall be paid by Merchant in accordance with the Member 
Bank Agreement. 
d. Retrieval Requests. Merchant is required by the Associations to store original 
documentation, and to timely respond to Retrieval Requests, of each Transaction 
for at least six months from the date of the respective Transaction, and to retain 
copies of all such data for at least 18 months from the date of the respective 
Transaction. Merchant is responsible for any Chargebacks that result from 
Merchant’s failure to timely respond to Retrieval Requests for documentation 
relating to a Transaction. 
4. FEES AND INVOICING 
a. Order Form. Merchant agrees to pay Tyler the fees set forth in or attached to the 
Order Form for services provided by Tyler and to which this Agreement is 
hyperlinked or attached. This may include fees for Payment Service Devices or 
other Equipment that Merchant has elected to purchase or rent as set forth on 
the Order Form. Fees for purchase will be invoiced upon shipment and Fees for 
rental will be invoiced annually in advance. All Fees due hereunder are due 
within 45 days of invoice. The terms and conditions of such purchase or rental 
are set forth on Exhibit B attached hereto and incorporated herein. 
b. Adjustments to Pricing. By giving written notice to Merchant, Tyler may change 
Merchant’s fees, charges and discounts resulting from (i) changes in Association 
fees (such as interchange, assessments and other charges); (ii) changes in 
pricing by any third party provider of a product or service used by Merchant; or 
(iii) other market adjustment. Such new prices shall be applicable as of the 
effective date established by the Association or third party provider, or as of any 
later date specified in Tyler’s notice to Merchant. In addition, Tyler may update 
pricing for rental of Equipment by giving written notice to Merchant at the end of 
any initial rental term or when such Equipment is upgraded to a newer model or

--- page 150 ---

4 
 
 
 
replaced in accordance with the pricing set forth on Tyler’s then-current Order 
Form. 
c. Payment of Fees. 
i. 
Online Payments. For payments that are initiated online, a 
convenience fee or service fee may be assessed to the Cardholder 
for each payment transaction that is paid electronically using a credit 
or debit card. Such convenience fee or service fee is set forth in the 
Order Form and will be charged at the time of the transaction to be 
deposited directly into a Tyler bank account from which all fees 
associated with processing and settling the Card Transactions will be 
paid. 
ii. 
Over the Counter Payments. For payments that are initiated in your 
offices, a service fee may be assessed to the Cardholder for each 
payment transaction as set forth in the Order Form, and such fees 
will be charged at the time of the transaction to be deposited directly 
into a Tyler bank account from which all fees associated with 
processing and settling the transactions will be paid. For all other 
fees, Tyler shall invoice Merchant for services and service fees on a 
monthly basis, unless otherwise set forth in the Order Form. Each 
invoice shall state the total invoiced amount and shall be 
accompanied by a reasonably detailed itemization of services and 
service fees. Following receipt of a properly submitted invoice, the 
Merchant shall pay amounts owing therein thirty (30) days in arrears. 
iii. 
Absorbed Payments. For payments that are initiated online and/or in- 
person, the Merchant may elect to pay for all fees related to the 
transaction including, without limitation, interchange fees, dues, 
assessments, card brand fees, and Tyler fees. 
iv. 
eCheck/ACH Payments. In addition, Tyler shall be authorized to 
charge eCheck/ACH fees and other fees specified in an Order Form 
to the end user. Unless otherwise set forth in the Order Form, fees 
will be charged at the time of the transaction to be deposited directly 
into a Tyler bank account.

12. TERM, SUSPENSION, AND 
TERMINATION 
a. Term. The term of this Processing Agreement (the “Term”) shall commence on 
the Effective Date and shall continue in effect for three years unless otherwise 
set forth on an Order Form; provided, however, that at the end of such initial 
term, and on each subsequent anniversary of the Effective Date, the term shall 
automatically extend for an additional year unless either party provides, at least 
ninety (90) days prior to the end of the then current term, written notice that it 
does not wish to extend the term or otherwise terminates the agreement for 
Cause pursuant to Section 12(b). Notwithstanding the foregoing, Tyler may elect 
to cease providing payment processing services upon the termination or 
expiration of Tyler’s other agreement with Merchant to provide Tyler software or 
services. 
b. Termination for Cause. Either party may terminate this Processing Agreement for 
Cause, provided that such party follows the procedures set forth in this Section 
(b). 
i. 
For purposes of this Section, “Cause” means either: 
A. a material breach of this Processing Agreement, which 
has not been cured within ninety (90) days of the date 
such party receives written notice of such breach; 
B. the failure by Merchant to timely pay when due any fees 
owed to Tyler pursuant to this Processing Agreement and 
any delinquent amounts remain outstanding for a period 
of thirty (30) days after Tyler provides written notice of its 
intent to terminate for failure to pay; 
C. breach of Section 7; or 
D. if Tyler becomes insolvent or bankrupt, or is the subject of 
any proceedings relating to its liquidation or insolvency or 
for the appointment of a receiver or similar officer for it, 
has a receiver of its assets or property appointed or 
makes an assignment for the benefit of all or substantially 
all of its creditors, or institutes or causes to be instituted 
any proceeding in bankruptcy or reorganization or 
rearrangement of its affairs. 
ii. 
No party may terminate this Processing Agreement under Section 12 
b(i)(A) unless it cooperates in good faith with the alleged breaching 
party during the cure period and complies in good faith with the 
dispute resolution procedures set forth in Section 13 following such 
period. 
iii. 
In the event either party terminates this Processing Agreement 
pursuant to this Section (b), each party shall return all products, 
documentation, confidential information, and other information 
disclosed or otherwise delivered to the other party prior to such 
termination, all revocable licenses shall terminate.

Any dispute arising out of, or relating to, this Processing Agreement that cannot be

Days at the Intermediary Dispute Level shall then be referred to Merchant’s chief

applicable division President (“Executive Dispute Level”), at such time and location 
reasonably designated by the parties. Any negotiations pursuant to this Section are 
confidential and shall be treated as compromise and settlement negotiations for 
purposes of the applicable rules of evidence. For any dispute that the parties are unable 
to resolve through informal discussions or negotiations or pursuant to the dispute 
resolution and escalation procedures set forth in this Processing Agreement, the parties 
shall submit the matter to non-binding mediation prior to the commencement of any 
legal proceeding. The foregoing shall not apply to claims for equitable relief under 
Section 7.

a. Assignment. Neither party may assign this Processing Agreement or any of its 
respective rights or obligations herein to any third party without the express 
written consent of the other party, which consent shall not be unreasonably 
withheld. 
b. Cumulative Remedies. Except as specifically provided herein, no remedy made 
available herein is intended to be exclusive of any other remedy, and each and 
every remedy shall be cumulative and shall be in addition to every other remedy 
provided herein or available at law or in equity. 
c. Notices. Except as otherwise expressly specified herein, all notices, requests or 
other communications shall be in writing and shall be deemed to have been 
given if delivered personally or mailed, by certified or registered mail, postage 
prepaid, return receipt requested, to the parties at their respective addresses set 
forth on the signature page hereto, or at such other addresses as may be

Agenda Number:  14
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR

TO:
City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
City Manager's Office
MEETING DATE:
June 03, 2024 
SUBJECT:
390 1st Avenue – Lease Amendment 
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve the 2nd amendment to the lease between the City and Tong Sui, LLC, for the City owned property at 390 1st 
Avenue to assign the lease to Antoine Patisserie, LLC, dba Anton SV Pâtisserie, under the existing lease terms; authorize a 
security deposit amount of $1,253.76; and authorize the City Manager to execute the amendment in substantially the 
form presented. 
BACKGROUND:
On October 12, 2021, the City Council approved the 1st amendment and an assignment of the lease to Tong Sui, LLC for 
the City owned property at 390 1st Avenue. The property is located in the Main Street garage on the corner of 1st Avenue 
adjacent to the train tracks. The retail space is approximately 355 square feet. Due to their expansion needs surpassing the 
space available, Tong Sui relocated from its location on 1st Avenue to 250 S B Street between 2nd and 3rd Avenues. Tong 
Sui closed its first location in early 2024 and has continued to meet its lease obligations to the City. 
Tong Sui does not need two locations in the Downtown and has identified Anton SV Pâtisserie as the assignee to take over 
the remaining four years of the lease, which will expire on June 30, 2028. Anton SV Pâtisserie is a bakery that specializes in 
mille crepe cakes and other desserts. A mille crepe is a layer cake made of crepes stacked with different fillings. Anton SV 
Pâtisserie is headquartered in San Jose, with fourteen pickup locations across the Bay Area, and will operate primarily as a 
take-out bakery. 
Prodesse Properties, the City’s commercial property manager, has performed the due diligence of evaluating Anton SV 
Pâtisserie and has concluded that it has adequate financial holdings and experience to operate a pickup location to 
Downtown San Mateo. Under the terms of the original lease agreement, the City may not unreasonably withhold its 
consent to a lease assignment. Accordingly, staff is proposing a second amendment to the lease to assign it to the new 
lessee; clarifying language stating prevailing wages must be paid for any improvements to the property because it is City-
owned; and collecting a security deposit of $1,253.76, equivalent to one month’s base rent. All other terms of the lease 
will remain the same. Once the assignment of the lease is completed, Anton SV Pâtisserie anticipates opening the facility in 
the summer of 2024.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The assignment and lease amendment will have no budget impact. The 2nd Lease Amendment will generate approximately 
$63,000 in rental income for the City over the course of the remaining term. Commercial property revenue funds the City’s 
expenses for operation, maintenance, and improvements to downtown parking facilities and are also used for street 
cleaning services. The revenue is deposited in the Downtown Parking and Maintenance Fund (Fund 28).

mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 
15301.)

DUPLICATE ORIGINAL

Premises: 390 First Ave, San Mateo, CA Date June 2018
Date (For reference only):, July 1, 2018

City of San Mateo ("Landlord") and Good Drink LLC dba Red Giant Coffee, a California, Limited Liability
Company ("Tenant") agree as follows:

1.

PROPERTY: Landlord rents to Tenant and Tenant rents from Landlord, the real property and improvements
described as: 390 1°’ Avenue San Mateo, CA 94401 ("Premises"), approximately 355 square feet, which comprise
approximately 9% of the total square footage of rentable space in the entire property. See Exhibit A for the
Premises location in the Main Street Garage and Exhibit B for a floor plan of the Premises.

BASE RENT: Tenant agrees to pay a monthly Base Rent ("Base Rent") at the rate of$1,050 per month, for the
first 12 months of the agreement. The base rent schedule shall be as follows:
From 7/1/2018 through 6/30/2019 the monthly base rent shall total $1,050.00
From 7/1/2019 through 6/30/2020 the monthly base rent shall total $1,081.50
From 7/1/2020through 6/30/2021 the monthly base rent shall total $1,113.95
From 7/1/2021 through 6/30/2022 the monthly base rent shall total $1,147.36
From 7/1/2022 through 6/30/2023 the monthly base rent shall total $1,181.78

(iv) Tenant causing, permitting, or suffering, without the prior written consent of Landlord, any act

C. Default Remedies: If an Event of Default shall occur and continue, then in addition to any other
remedies available to Landlord at law or in equity, Landlord shall have the immediate option to terminate
this Lease and bring suit against Tenant and recover as an award in such suit the following:

(i) the worth at the time of award of the unpaid Rent and all other sums due hereunder which had
been earned at the time of termination;

(ii) the worth at the time of award of the amount by which the unpaid Rent and all other sums due
hereunder which would have been earned after termination until the time of award exceeds the
amount of such rental loss that Tenant proves could have been reasonably avoided;

(iii) the worth at the time of award of the amount by which the unpaid Rent and all other sums due
hereunder for the balance of the Term after termination exceeds the amount of such rental loss
that Tenant proves could be reasonably avoided;

(iv) any other amount necessary to compensate Landlord for all the detriment proximately caused by
Tenant's failure to perform its obligations under this Lease; and

(v) such amounts in addition to or in lieu of the foregoing as may be permitted from time to time by
applicable California law.

DAMAGE TO PREMISES: If, by no fault of Tenant, Premises are totally or partially damaged or destroyed
by fire, earthquake, accident or other casualty, Landlord shall have the right to restore the Premises by repair or
rebuilding. If Landlord elects to repair or rebuild, and is able to complete such restoration within 90 days from
the date of damage, subject to the terms of this section, this agreement shall remain in full force and effect. If
Landlord is unable to restore the Premises within this time, or if Landlord elects not to restore, then either
Landlord or Tenant may terminate this agreement by giving the other written notice. Rent shall be abated as of
the date of damage. The abated amount shall be the current monthly Rent prorated on a 30-day basis. If this
agreement is not terminated, and the damage is not repaired, then Rent shall be reduced based on the extent to
which the damage interferes with Tenant's reasonable use of Premises. If damage occurs as a result of an act of
Tenant or Tenant's guests, only Landlord shall have the right of termination, and no reduction in Rent shall be
made.

HAZARDOUS MATERIALS: Tenant shall not use, store, generate, release or dispose of any hazardous
material on the Premises or the property of which the Premises are part. However, Tenant is permitted to make
use of such materials that are required to be used in the normal course of Tenant's business provided that Tenant
complies with all applicable Laws related to the hazardous materials. Tenant is responsible for the cost of
removal and remediation, or any clean-up of any contamination caused by Tenant.

agreement as of the date possession is given to the condemner. All condemnation proceeds, exclusive of those
allocated by the condemner to Tenant's relocation costs and trade fixtures, belong to Landlord.

27. INDEMNIFICATION: Tenant agrees to indemnify, and hold harmless Landlord, and its officers, officials,
agents, and employees, from any and all liabilities, claims, demands, actions, losses, damages, and costs,
including all costs of defense thereof and any award of attorney’s fees, caused by, arising out of, or in any way
related to Tenant’s use or occupancy of the leased premises. Tenant agrees to defend landlord against any such
claims.

28. INSURANCE: Tenant shall procure and maintain for the duration of the Lease insurance against claims for
injuries to persons or damages to property which may arise from or in connection with the Tenant’s operation
and use of the leased premises, as described in this section. The cost of such insurance shall be borne by the
Tenant.

A. Minimum Scope Of Insurance:
(i) Insurance Services Office Commercial General Liability coverage (occurrence form CG 0001).

(ii) Workers’ compensation insurance as required by the State of California and Employer’s Liability
insurance (for tenants with employees).

(iii) Property insurance against all risks of loss to any tenant improvements or betterments.

B. Minimum Limits Of Insurance: Tenant shall maintain limits no less than:

(i) General liability: $2,000,000 per occurrence for bodily injury, personal injury and property
damage. If Commercial General Liability Insurance or other form with a general aggregate limit
is used, either the general aggregate limit shall apply separately to this project/location or the
general aggregate limit shall be twice the required occurrence limit.

(ii) Employer’s liability: $1,000,000 per accident for bodily injury or disease.
(iii) Property insurance: Full replacement cost with no coinsurance penalty provision.

C. Deductibles And Self-Insured Retentions: Any deductibles or self-insured retentions must be
declared to and approved by the Landlord. At the option of the Landlord, either: The insurer shall
reduce or eliminate such deductibles or self-insured retentions as respects the Landlord, its officers,
officials, agents, and employees; or the Tenant shall provide a financial guarantee satisfactory to the
Landlord guaranteeing payment of losses and related investigations, claim administration, and defense
expenses.

D. Other Insurance Provisions: The general liability policy is to contain, or be endorsed to contain, the
following provisions:

(i) The Landlord, its officers, officials, agents, and employees are to be covered as insureds with
respect to liability arising out of ownership, maintenance or use of that part of the premises
leased to the Tenant.

(ii) The Tenant’s insurance coverage shall be primary insurance as respects the Landlord, its
officers, officials, agents, and employees. Any insurance or self-insurance maintained by the
Landlord, its officers, officials, agents and employees shall be excess of the Tenant’s insurance
and shall not contribute with it.

(iii) Each insurance policy required by this clause shall be endorsed to state that coverage shall not
be canceled, except after 30 days’ prior written notice by certified mail, return receipt requested,
has been given to the Landlord.

E. Acceptability Of Insurer: Insurance is to be placed with insurers with a current A.M. Best’s rating of
no less than A: VII.

action; (iii) the filing or enforcement of a mechanic's lien; (iv) any matter that is within the jurisdiction

MEETING DATE:
June 03, 2024 
SUBJECT:
Citywide Complete Streets Plan – Update
RECOMMENDATION:
Receive an update on the San Mateo Citywide Complete Streets Plan and provide feedback.
BACKGROUND:
The City was awarded approximately $490,000 from the Caltrans Sustainable Communities grant program to fund the San 
Mateo Complete Streets Plan (“Plan”). The Plan will complement the City’s General Plan by creating an actionable plan 
rooted in safety for all transportation modes and will result in policies, goals, and prioritized projects that are focused on 
improving mobility, equity, connectivity, and sustainability to build a better circulation network for the City’s future. The 
Plan will provide the basis for projects that are planned, designed, constructed, and maintained for all roadway users, 
allowing the City to develop a safe mobility network for many years to come. The final outcome of this effort will be an 
adopted Citywide Complete Streets Plan and a Design Standards Manual. The Citywide Complete Streets Plan effort began 
in November 2022.  To ensure the final Complete Streets Plan is consistent with Council’s vision and expectations, staff is 
bringing different components for Council ’s review and feedback as they are developed.  This presentation will cover work 
to-date on community engagement and the current approach to establishing modal priorities for City roadways.  
Community Engagement 
Given the nature of the project, community engagement has been a key component to provide information and direction 
for this project. Based on prior Council feedback, Staff and the consultant team have worked through a three (3) phase 
community engagement effort. The first phase of community engagement focused on learning about transportation needs 
and concerns in the community through stakeholder interviews, focus groups, active engagement tours, and pop-up 
events. Phase 1 included workshops conducted in Spanish and workshops with both English and Spanish speakers where 
simultaneous translation was provided and utilized. Since this item was last brought for Council feedback on October 16, 
2023, staff and the consultant team have completed Phases 2 and 3 of community engagement.  These phases of 
engagement included the following and are summarized in greater detail in Attachments 1 and 2. 
•
Community Engagement: In Phase 2 of community engagement, the project team focused on leveraging 
connections with the community and the San Mateo-Foster City school district to plan and organize targeted focus 
groups and workshops to gain insight on specific resident concerns regarding transportation. The team also 
utilized existing events to engage with people where they recreate or congregate, to gather input from residents 
and roadway users from all parts of the City. This included tabling at September Nights on B Street, focus groups 
with Parent Teacher Association (PTA) members at Baywood and Sunnybrae Elementary Schools and with Hillsdale 
High School students, and a meeting with Shoreview-Parkside residents. The focus groups, given the concentrated 
audiences, were advertised directly to the school communities and residents through coordination with school 
administrators and neighborhood leaders. 
188 of 465

--- page 189 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
During Phase 3 of engagement, City staff and the consultant team hosted three (3) in-person community 
workshops throughout the City’s five council districts. Following the successful implementation of district-focused 
workshops for the General Plan 2040, hosting the workshops in this manner provided engagement opportunities 
nearer to residents' homes, and ability for Councilmembers to more deeply engage with the project. Staff 
advertised the workshops to attendees via the City’s e-newsletter, the City’s social media channels, emails to 
neighborhood associations and school stakeholders, flyers for print in multiple languages, and information on the 
City’s website. Each workshop consisted of an open-house format that was modeled on prior successful 
engagement showcasing maps of potential improvements along the Plan’s ten (10) identified priority corridors. A 
presentation was offered midway through the open house to more fully explain the project, with opportunity for 
Q&A. In response to feedback that residents and other stakeholders appreciate opportunities to participate 
virtually when unable to attend in-person meetings, staff provided an online survey modeled on the open house to 
allow similar in-depth comments on each priority corridor. The workshops offered simultaneous Spanish 
translation, and the survey was available in Spanish as well. 
•
Feedback: The community pop-up event, focus groups, and workshop in Phase 2 provided insight into resident 
concerns about moving around San Mateo. Some general trends included safety such as traffic safety, speeding, 
and non-compliance with the rules of the road, concerns about emergency preparedness as it relates to 
transportation, and a desire to see more pedestrian-friendly infrastructure and safety enhancements.
Phase 3 feedback focused on offering residents opportunity to provide feedback on the priority corridor projects. 
Generally, residents were supportive of bicycle and pedestrian safety improvements and efforts to reduce speeds 
for vehicles, with mixed feedback on the conversion of vehicle travel lanes and/or parking for dedicated bus 
and/or bike lanes. There was also support for enhanced signage and east-west connectivity for pedestrians and 
bicyclists, particularly across US 101. Feedback from the workshops and survey will be incorporated into the 
corridor recommendations in the Plan. 
Street Typologies and Modal Priorities 
Staff and the consultant team developed four key policies guiding the creation of the Plan, and the Sustainability and 
Infrastructure Commission and City Council confirmed these policies: 
•
Prioritize Safety for All Modes
•
Rebalance Priorities
•
Fund and Implement Projects, and 
•
Engage our Communities.
As part of the Rebalance Priorities policy, City staff and the consultant team developed a methodology to utilize street 
characteristics and adjacent land uses to identify modal priorities for roadways throughout the City. Determining modal 
prioritization based on the width of the roadway available and the land uses that are primarily present enables staff and 
others to more consistently allocate available right-of-way as well as make operational decisions based on the modal 
priorities. In having this information available when designing future projects, staff can identify the intended modal 
priority for a given roadway and design improvements based on those priorities ahead of time, rather than identifying 
priorities on a project-by-project basis that often results in inconsistency. This piecemeal approach is how the roadway 
design process is currently completed, but it results in inconsistencies in active transportation implementation. 
First, land use types have been identified as neighborhood, mixed-use, and commercial based on the land uses designated 
in the recently adopted General Plan 2040. 
•
Neighborhood: Primarily residential, with schools, parks, and some small businesses. Multimodal safety and urban 
greening are prioritized with a balanced approach to residential parking management. 
•
Mixed-Use: Characterizes newly developing neighborhoods and transit-oriented communities. These areas are 
highly walkable with multimodal access to higher density homes and businesses. 
•
Commercial: Larger businesses less oriented to the street, including malls and office parks. Circulation is focused 
189 of 465

--- page 190 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
on enhancing safety and multimodal access. Also includes service areas with light industrial uses. 
Generally, streets have been identified as compact, intermediate, or broad based on existing street widths; these 
designations in combination with adjacent land uses will be used to identify specific types of implementations in the 
Complete Streets Plan. While it is anticipated that these designations may lend to modifications in Caltrans-specified 
roadway classifications, they are not intended as a one-for-one replacement. 
•
Compact: Very narrow roadways, providing local access to homes and businesses. 
•
Intermediate: Midsize roadways that provide circulation across land use contexts, with multi-modal needs 
strategically prioritized based on modal networks. 
•
Broad: Very wide roadways that carry more multimodal circulation and have high need for safety management.
The combination of land use type and roadway width provide the street typology, which aligns with design specifications 
in the Design Standards Manual. For example, a roadway classified as mixed-use intermediate would align with certain 
lane widths, bike facility types and widths, and sidewalk requirements that are all outlined in the Manual. 
Street typologies were utilized to develop modal priorities, or transportation modes that are prioritized for that type of 
roadway and are crucial in determining the types of tools that may be used on each corridor.  Staff will summarize the 
approach to assigning modal priorities to each roadway, but in general, it starts from a framework of specific modal 
priorities being assigned to each category of land use type/street typology and is then refined based on information in 
existing transportation plans, local context, general city circulation goals, etc.  A modal priority may be pedestrian, transit, 
bike, or auto; not having a certain modal priority for a roadway does not mean the mode will not exist on that roadway. 
Rather, it means that people utilizing the priority mode need additional support for safe mobility and access. 
In creating general modal priorities based on land use, lane width, and roadway characteristics, the Complete Streets Plan 
provides detail on what infrastructure improvements and enhancements should be prioritized across the City. In practice, 
this allows the City to prioritize modes on roadways based on common characteristics, rather than on an individual project 
level basis, and provides continuity and consistency in design and implementation. Some examples of proposed modal 
priorities include the following. 
•
Neighborhood Streets: Safety is prioritized for all users on these streets, including those who live, walk, bike, drive, 
take transit, and play there. Design on these roadways will focus on safety for all modes, and speed management. 
•
Bicycle and Pedestrian Priority: These roadways will prioritize bike/pedestrian transportation, indicating these 
modes need additional support for safety on these corridors. This does not preclude or remove autos from the 
corridor. 
•
Automobile and Bicycle Priority: Roadways with specific characteristics, like those that cross US 101, have modal 
priorities for bicycles and autos to facilitate and enhance safe connectivity for these modes given the limited 
connectivity across these large barriers. 
Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission Feedback
Staff presented this information to the Sustainability and Infrastructure Commission during the May 8, 2024, meeting. 
Commission feedback included the following.
•
Bicycle and auto connectivity on east-west corridors is important for circulation but difficult with limited roadway 
widths.
•
Be mindful of potential parking removal in projects and identify that early in the design process.
•
Maintaining north and south access into the Downtown is important.
•
Commissioners supported safety for all modes on neighborhood streets.
•
Consider a second-tier priority for bicycles on El Camino Real if feasible.
Requested Feedback and Next Steps 
To ensure Council consensus on the approach to assigning modal priorities to City roadways, staff is seeking feedback on 
the following questions:  
190 of 465

--- page 191 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
1.
Does Council have feedback on how the street typologies were developed?
2.
Does Council have feedback on how modal priorities were assigned to each street typology?
3.
Does Council have feedback on the resulting modal priorities map?
Staff and the consultant team will incorporate feedback from the Council and Commission, in addition to community 
feedback. Staff expects to bring the additional elements of the Complete Street Plan for Commission and Council feedback 
in summer 2024, with the draft Plan being prepared for review later in 2024.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budgetary impact associated with the recommendation of this agenda report. The funding for the Plan is 
budgeted in the Complete Streets Plan Project (46R014) and is provided in part through a Caltrans Sustainable 
Communities grant with local matching funds. 
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Complete Streets Plan update is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative 
activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 
15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

ACTIVITY INSIGHTS
September Nights on B Street (22 participants)
Baywood Elementary PTA Meeting (20 participants)
Key highlights gathered from specific 
engagement activities
•
Emphasizing the importance of educating bicyclists, pedestrians, 
and drivers on road rules to improve safety and cooperation among 
all road users.
•
Introducing first and last mile transit solutions, improving SamTrans 
frequency and reliability, and tackling congestion and parking 
challenges associated with new developments.
•
Introduction of pedestrian and bicyclist visibility measures, including 
advanced crosswalk signals and flashing beacons, coupled with 
speed deterrence infrastructure such as roundabouts and speed 
bumps to enhance street safety and manage parking congestion.
•
Need to address illegal U-turns and speeding, particularly during 
school hours around Alameda de las Pulgas.
•
Participants suggested the installation of more stop signs or 
signals to effectively reduce speeding in the area.
•
Emphasized the need for improved coordination between city 
officials, schools, and construction authorities to avoid scheduling 
conflicts during critical school hours. There was interest in 
understanding why the school hasn't been included in the 'Safe 
Routes to School' program
195 of 465

--- page 196 ---
ACTIVITY INSIGHTS
Sunnybrae Elementary Parent Focus Group
(15 participants)
Hillsdale High School Student Focus Group
(~ 14 participants)
Key highlights gathered from specific 
engagement activities (continued)
•
There is a need for more safety infrastructure to ensure bikers and 
pedestrians are better seen at busy corridors and intersections.
•
There is a need for more connections on the commute to and 
from school and at key City destinations such as Hillsdale Mall and 
the Hillsdale Caltrain Station
•
There is a recognized need for additional painting on curbs near 
intersections to prevent parking that obstructs visibility.
•
Concerns about speeding vehicles, leading to a call for more 
enforcement to ensure safer roads. Additionally, parents lack 
confidence in allowing their children to travel to school alone, 
following incidents where children were hit/nearly hit by vehicles.
•
Timing of road construction, sweeping, and maintenance needs 
better coordination with the city and schools.
196 of 465

--- page 197 ---
ACTIVITY INSIGHTS
Shoreview-Parkside Meeting
(~ 30 participants)
Key highlights gathered from specific 
engagement activities (continued)
•
Key discussions revolved around tackling speeding, stop sign 
violations, and poor intersection visibility. Solutions proposed were 
flashing stop signs near schools, better street sign visibility, speed 
bumps, and coordinated traffic control with schools.
•
Emphasis was placed on improving east-west neighborhood 
connectivity. Suggestions included constructing safer pedestrian 
bridges, shuttle services to reduce traffic, and integrating 
pedestrian, bike, and vehicle traffic safely, particularly in 
congested areas.
•
Concerns were raised about the safety of bicyclists and 
pedestrians in high-traffic and school zones. Proposals focused on 
creating dedicated bike lanes, redesigning bike trails for safety, 
and ensuring ADA compliance for bus stops. Reevaluating the 
Fashion Island Blvd bike lane was also considered.
•
The importance of community engagement in public safety and 
preparedness for emergencies like earthquakes or tsunamis was 
highlighted. This included public safety campaigns and planning 
evacuation routes.

7
PEDESTRIAN NETWORK
•
Intersection safety: Residents expressed concerns about dangerous 
intersections emphasizing the need for additional safety measures.
•
Pedestrian crossings: Community members highlight difficulties in crossing 
major roads like El Camino Real during daylight hours, suggesting the 
installation of more crosswalks and stop signs.
•
Infrastructure visibility: Faded stop sign street signage throughout Parkside 
raises visibility concerns, calling for measures like red paint on corners to 
prevent parking and enhance safety.
•
General safety: Overall, there were requests for improved safety and 
pedestrian-friendly infrastructure, encompassing diverse issues such as 
crosswalks, stop signs, and street maintenance.
General themes from community feedback
198 of 465

--- page 199 ---
8
BICYCLE NETWORK
•
Infrastructure safety: Residents emphasize the need for safety measures in 
bike infrastructure, including improved signage and dedicated bike lanes in 
high-traffic areas and at unsafe intersections.
•
Connectivity: Connectivity: Calls for better bike connectivity, such as new bike 
paths near the Boys and Girls Club in the North Shoreview neighborhood, 
highlight the importance of expanding the bike network.
•
Trail promotion: Community members called for collaboration with the City of 
San Mateo to create new bike trails, accompanied by the installation of bike 
stop lights at critical intersections. This suggestion underscores the 
importance of actively promoting and expanding the city's network of bike 
trails.
•
Speed deterrence: Improving the effectiveness of sharrows/bike boulevards 
on residential streets to prevent speeding on long city blocks is 
recommended, focusing on speed deterrence infrastructure.

High Need Corridor Comments
1. 31st Avenue (4) - General speeding concerns, making it unsafe for 
pedestrians/cyclists
2. 3rd Avenue/J Hart Clinton Dr (7) - Many commercial vehicles parked; inconsistent 
bike lanes, especially crossing 3rd from east (merges onto sidewalk)
3. Alameda de Las Pulgas (10)  - Curves and hills near schools creates dangerous 
crossing and travel conditions for drivers, pedestrians, and bicyclists.
4. El Camino Real (5) - Maintenance, visibility, and bicycle/pedestrian safety concerns
5. Fashion Island Blvd (6) - high congestion; ingress/egress onto 101 is dangerous for 
bicyclists to cross
6. Grant St (2) - Need for better safety measures for pedestrians and bicyclists.
7. Hillsdale Blvd (7)- dangerous conditions for pedestrians and bicyclists
8. Monte Diablo Ave (2) - Need for improved visibility, lighting, and maintenance
9. Norfolk St (7) - unsafe intersections and mobility for bikes; need of infrastructure 
improvements
10.Poplar Ave (1) - Narrow streets, many cars parked on sidewalk
Top ten corridors identified in Phase 1 as high need are confirmed by

MAIN THEMES FROM SURVEY
•
Mixed input on conversion of vehicular lane travel and/or parking for dedicated bus and/or 
bike lanes with appreciation for need for faster transit times and increased safety for 
bicyclists but concerns for impact on parking availability and traffic congestion.
•
General support for pedestrian and bicyclist safety improvements (such as protected lanes, 
crosswalks, speed bumps, and increased visibility) and efforts to slow down vehicular 
speeding, especially on large roadways. Some concern over curb extension impact on 
parking.
•
General support for addition of traffic signals, traffic signal synchronization and protected 
turn lanes for vehicles.
•
Support for better wayfinding and east-west connectivity for pedestrians and bicyclists, 
especially across Highway 101.
